  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5aa5ab69-5d89-425a-9e41-4e25d31a3e71'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText12735614439796137159" style="display:none">Dana attends a school of magic with only one other student. She has a great love only she can see. And only she can unravel these mysteries and become mistress of the Valley of the Wolves.<br /><br />Ever since Dana was a little girl, Kai has been her best friend and constant companion--even though she's the only one who can see him. Then the mysterious Maestro comes to her farm and offers her the opportunity of a lifetime: the chance to study sorcery in the Valley of the Wolves. And Dana knows she must go, for the Maestro can see Kai too....<br /> At age 27, Laura Gallego Garcia is already Spain's answer to J. K. Rowling, creating fantasies rich with magic and meaning. This is her most popular novel, a book for every kid who's ever felt set apart and everyone who finds a place all their own.</span>

<div id="review_123672682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123672682" />
    <a title="Begonia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4340283-begonia"><img alt="Begonia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285526453p2/4340283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123672682?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Begonia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Begonia" href="/user/show/4340283-begonia">Begonia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123672682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5478325143744948488">I read this book when i was a child (I think I was about 8 or 9 years old).I read it in less than three days.I know,you may say that's not a big deal because the book isn't very long but then,and for a kid of my age,it was more than enough.<br/>The thing is that I really loved this book for many reasons, including the simple but formidable prose,the characters' tenderness,the friendship between Kai and Dana,etc.<br/>Highly recommended,specially for children.<br/><br/>------------------------------------------------</span>
  <span id="freeText5478325143744948488" style="display:none">I read this book when i was a child (I think I was about 8 or 9 years old).I read it in less than three days.I know,you may say that's not a big deal because the book isn't very long but then,and for a kid of my age,it was more than enough.<br />The thing is that I really loved this book for many reasons, including the simple but formidable prose,the characters' tenderness,the friendship between Kai and Dana,etc.<br />Highly recommended,specially for children.<br /><br />-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />Leí este libro de niña,creo que tenía unos ocho o nueve años cuando cayó en mis manos.Lo devoré en menos de tres días.Se que no es una gran hazaña ya que el libro no es excesivamente largo pero por aquel entonces y para una cría de mi edad,era más que suficiente (aunque esperé con gran impaciencia la segunda parte).<br />La cuestion esque este libro me encantó por muchas razones,como la sencilla pero formidable prosa de Laura,la ternura de los personajes,el valor que se le da a la amistad,etc.<br />Muy recomendable para todos los públicos pero especialmente para niños. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5478325143744948488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11139008395554744115">This is about a girl who can see spirits and an evil man sees this in her and takes her away from her home which is suffering from drought. She has an "imaginary" friend since she was young but he's really one of the spirits sent to help her until his time of dead. They all go to live with the evil magician but one day a grand lady appears to her and won't go away. The grand lady is also another spirit and needs her help to defeat the evil magician. So they do but in order for her to defeat him </span>
  <span id="freeText11139008395554744115" style="display:none">This is about a girl who can see spirits and an evil man sees this in her and takes her away from her home which is suffering from drought. She has an "imaginary" friend since she was young but he's really one of the spirits sent to help her until his time of dead. They all go to live with the evil magician but one day a grand lady appears to her and won't go away. The grand lady is also another spirit and needs her help to defeat the evil magician. So they do but in order for her to defeat him she has to die first and then come back to life which she can because she is the doorway to the spirit world. She wants to stay in the world of the dead to be with her Spirit friend but he made her go back to live out her life until its her time to die and then they can be together.<br />The girl has to learn what are her most important choices in life and to live every ounce of it until it's her time because of her promise to Kai, her spirit friend.</span>

  <span id="freeText17826092794147964605" style="display:none">• Title and Author: <br />El Valle de los Lobos, Laura Gallego<br />• Main characters: <br />Dana has been chosen to become a wizard in the wolf valley. Kai, the ghost, best friend of Dana. Marietta, the cooker of the tower. The professor, the director of the academy. <br />• Summary of the plot:<br />Dana grew up with her brothers and sisters as one more, however everybody knew that she was different, she saw things that others did not see, and his best friend was a ghost, Kai. His life changed forever when the professor appeared and took her to the Tower, in the Valley of the wolves, where there was a curse. There she grew and learned how to become a wizard. Everything goes well until a ghost appear to her asking for help, and Dana helped her. <br />• Summary of the conflict:<br />Dana is trying to help the ghost. She decided to go to the valley at night. But there is a curse in the valley, she went to the valley, and saw what she was looking for, when the wolves came for her, and start attacking her. Next day she woke up at the tower, and what she only remembered was that she went to the valley and almost died. She keeps on thinking on what happened and decided to go again, but this time with help. She asked her only classmate and he agree to go. The night didn't go well, because they almost die again. When she woke up again she didn't remembered anything again. <br />At the end she founds what she wanted and realized that the professor was bad. He killed the women that appear to her, so she put the curse on the valley. <br />• Conclusion <br />I read this book because the author has written a few books that I liked. However this book wasn't one of my favorites. It wasn't a very good book because it was saying always the same, and repeating things that weren't important, instead of talking more about the main idea of the book.</span>

<div id="review_1774434473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774434473" />
    <a title="Mari Degard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15929796-mari-degard"><img alt="Mari Degard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460171377p2/15929796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774434473?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari Degard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari Degard" href="/user/show/15929796-mari-degard">Mari Degard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15929796-mari-degard?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774434473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13816303915549243412">After some research I noticed that this was the author's first published book, which kind of comes as expected after reading it. One of the things that bothered me the most was that the prose was unplanned, bland and explanatory in the least interesting parts. She explains how a girl meets a strange boy and they suddenly become best friends forever in less than four paragraphs and then uses the whole epilogue to provide you with the background story of the villain. <br/>Saying that she was rushing th</span>
  <span id="freeText13816303915549243412" style="display:none">After some research I noticed that this was the author's first published book, which kind of comes as expected after reading it. One of the things that bothered me the most was that the prose was unplanned, bland and explanatory in the least interesting parts. She explains how a girl meets a strange boy and they suddenly become best friends forever in less than four paragraphs and then uses the whole epilogue to provide you with the background story of the villain. <br />Saying that she was rushing things out while writing this story is an understatement. It is obvious that her first novel was pretty much a writing experiment. Still, I believe that like any author she must have shown progress along the rest of her books (which I still have to read) so if you have read other books from her and liked them I'd recommend you not to expect the same quality from this one. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13816303915549243412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183483165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1941109925846758563">Well, this wasn't the most amazing book ever, but I liked it. The frustrating thing is that it was translated from Spanish six years after being published. And the rest of the series still hasn't been translated. And...I don't speak Spanish. So now I'm rather upset, because it's quite cruel to translate the first book ONLY. Meh. I guess I'll have to learn Spanish so I can read the rest of this series. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2555207615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555207615" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85360819-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555207615?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/85360819-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555207615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13381310121713925444">When I started reading this book, I had no idea that this was originally in Spanish. If I didn't know that this was translated from Spanish to English, my opinion would be way more harsh. Usually books that have been translated miss out from the literary devices that could have been used. Maybe in Spanish this book would have given me a better feel, however I don't speak Spanish and may never read the actual version. I'm just going to judge the English version. What really annoyed me was the lac</span>
  <span id="freeText13381310121713925444" style="display:none">When I started reading this book, I had no idea that this was originally in Spanish. If I didn't know that this was translated from Spanish to English, my opinion would be way more harsh. Usually books that have been translated miss out from the literary devices that could have been used. Maybe in Spanish this book would have given me a better feel, however I don't speak Spanish and may never read the actual version. I'm just going to judge the English version. What really annoyed me was the lack of descriptions. Me, personally, love books with great descriptions and use of literary devices because they make me more interested in the book. However, in this book, there are descriptions that are enough to keep the story moving, but no enough to make me feel like I constantly need to know what would happen next. For example, "After a moment, he smiled, and Dana relaxed; but she knew intuitively that however closely their souls might be united, a perplexing abyss lay between them." It may sound descriptive, but it doesn't speak to you like it's rich enough. It just doesn't hit you enough that you want to know about that metaphorical abyss. The transitioning of how time works isn't all too great either. For example, right after the quote, "One gray, cloudy day after doing chores, Dana and Kai ran to the forest." It just doesn't make sense to me that right after a part questioning Kai and Dana's unity, it just transitions right away to a new day, like nothing just happened from the previous scene. However, this book delivered that it's a fantasy book that's a pretty quick and decent read. I'm just picky about how the language is presented. I would recommend this book 5th to 8th graders because it will give the satisfaction of reading a fantasy book to mainly young readers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13381310121713925444" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9683232805264960048">This book captivated me on my first reading. I was fascinated by Dana and the ghost boy Kai (afterwards I was desperate to read more May-December ghost romances), and intrigued by Dana's relationship with the mysterious Maestro, who mentors Dana even while Dana slowly realizes that she must not be so in awe of him and that she must find out his secrets and confront him someday. Dana is driven and focused, and her independence and insularity is her biggest weakness that she must overcome, and eve</span>
  <span id="freeText9683232805264960048" style="display:none">This book captivated me on my first reading. I was fascinated by Dana and the ghost boy Kai (afterwards I was desperate to read more May-December ghost romances), and intrigued by Dana's relationship with the mysterious Maestro, who mentors Dana even while Dana slowly realizes that she must not be so in awe of him and that she must find out his secrets and confront him someday. Dana is driven and focused, and her independence and insularity is her biggest weakness that she must overcome, and eventually she does realize that she needs allies and more than that, friends who push her to be better and take notice of what is actually important. Dana's character really connected with me, as I am a similarly independent and semi-oblivious person who struggles to make personal connections, but when they are formed, they run very deep. To twelve-year-old me, the ending was heartbreaking.<br /><br />How I wish the rest of the series was translated! It has been so long since that first reading, and I still remember this story vividly.</span>

<div id="review_872647135" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/872647135" />
    <a title="Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6904180-elena"><img alt="Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599645052p2/6904180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/872647135?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elena" href="/user/show/6904180-elena">Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788434873612" href="/book/show/2797676-el-valle-de-los-lobos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6904180-elena?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6904180-elena?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872647135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9807857225613300746"><i>(Sigue leyendo para encontrar la reseña en español)</i><br/><br/>This is a very interesting story and I liked it a lot. We see the story through the point of view of Dana, with only a few scenes showing something that Dana is not seeing. <br/><br/>Kai is probably the most interesting character, because he’s something that doesn’t seem possible, even in a world where magic and dragons exist. He first appears as Dana’s friend and we learn later that nobody else can see him. There are also other mysterious characters, who</span>
  <span id="freeText9807857225613300746" style="display:none"><i>(Sigue leyendo para encontrar la reseña en español)</i><br /><br />This is a very interesting story and I liked it a lot. We see the story through the point of view of Dana, with only a few scenes showing something that Dana is not seeing. <br /><br />Kai is probably the most interesting character, because he’s something that doesn’t seem possible, even in a world where magic and dragons exist. He first appears as Dana’s friend and we learn later that nobody else can see him. There are also other mysterious characters, who know more than they’re saying. Even the ones that look innocent and unimportant are hiding something. Then we have the wolves, that are more than just normal wolves. They stay away from the tower and only appear at night, but they have a special connection to one of the characters. This is the only part that I didn’t like so much, because the name of that character already implies that wolves are part of his life.<br /><br />One thing that I really liked, is that the author doesn’t spend pages and pages describing races and cultures -not that there are that many either, but still- and the book is more focused on the plot. <br /><br />There are some good plot twists and the mystery will leave the reader wanting to keep on reading until the end. It’s a fast read with under 300 pages, but very enjoyable, and I would recommend it to anyone who likes fantasy.<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />Es una historia muy interesante que me gustó mucho. Vemos la acción desde el punto de vista de Dana, con sólo unas pocas escenas mostrando algo the Dana no está viendo. <br /><br />Kai es probablemente el personaje más interesante, porque es algo que no debería ser posible, incluso en un mundo donde la magia y los dragones existen. Primero aparece como el amigo de Dana y más tarde descubrimos que nadie más lo puede ver. Hay también otros personajes misteriosos, que sabe más de lo que cuentan. Incluso los que parecen inocentes y poco importantes están escondiendo algo. Luego están los lobos, que son más que lobos normales. Se mantienen alejados de la torre y sólo aparecen de noche, pero tiene una conexión especial con uno de los personajes. Esta es la parte que no me gustó tanto, porque el nombre de ese personaje ya indica que los lobos son parte de su vida.<br /><br />Una cosa que me gustó mucho es que la autora no usa páginas y páginas para describir las distintas razas y culturas -tampoco es que haya tantas, pero aún así- y el libro está más centrado en el argumento.<br /><br />Hay buenos giros inesperados y el misterio deja al lector queriendo continuar leyendo hasta el final. Es una lectura bastante rápida, con menos de 300 páginas, pero muy agradable y la recomiendo a toda persona que le guste la fantasía.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9807857225613300746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30110260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30110260" />
    <a title="Roxane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1148105-roxane"><img alt="Roxane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519370095p2/1148105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30110260?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxane" href="/user/show/1148105-roxane">Roxane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9788467508895" href="/book/show/2188353.El_valle_de_los_lobos">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1148105-roxane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1148105-roxane?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1148105-roxane?shelf=spanish">spanish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30110260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9460851266441807266">This is the first novel I've ever read in Spanish, so this was somewhat of a personal challenge. I'm glad to say that I read all of its 317 pages (and that doesn't include the pages in my dictionary) in less than a week. It just might be back on speaking terms with Spanish. Anyway I am very eager to read the rest of the trilogy as well as the prequel. <br/><br/>Everyone knew that Dana was different though they all treated her the same as everyone else. She never played much with others, spending most of h</span>
  <span id="freeText9460851266441807266" style="display:none">This is the first novel I've ever read in Spanish, so this was somewhat of a personal challenge. I'm glad to say that I read all of its 317 pages (and that doesn't include the pages in my dictionary) in less than a week. It just might be back on speaking terms with Spanish. Anyway I am very eager to read the rest of the trilogy as well as the prequel. <br /><br />Everyone knew that Dana was different though they all treated her the same as everyone else. She never played much with others, spending most of her time on her own... or rather with her friend Kai that no one else seems aware of. One day, a wizard of the first order comes to take her away from her family and farmer's life to have her attend the famous school of witchcraft of The Tower. Dana's world changes forever a she begins to understand just how special she is and that things aren't always what they seem.<br /><br />A traditional children's fantasy book the likes of many and yet a very entertaining read all the way through. The main plot and various subplots as well the general pace of the book could easily have made it a young adult novel. The writing however makes it pretty clear that it is a book aimed at a younger audience... which is all very well because otherwise I wouldn't have picked it up in Spanish. The vocabulary is purposefully limited and pretty accessible.<br /><br />Nevertheless, the trilogy is a bestseller in Spain and as far as I know, it's been translated in French and English. It's a wonderful and touching fantasy tale which will not fail to delight young readers. While the book's premises are typical of traditional fantasy (wizards, unicorns, elves, dwarfs, etc.), it's overall different enough to grab the reader's attention to the very last page.<br /><br />Recommended for young readers.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9460851266441807266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_678252533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/678252533" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2401540-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/678252533?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2401540-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer678252533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5093192282265223972">I read this because several of my preteens/teens were reading it and I had not heard much about this title. <br/>Dana is a quiet girl who spends all of her time with her friend Kai, a boy her age who can't be seen by anyone but Dana. At a young age, Dana is taken away by a strange man (with the consent of her parents). The man promises to keep her safe and feed her, which is more than her parents are able to guarantee. They travel for several days to the man's residence -- a lonely tower -- where the</span>
  <span id="freeText5093192282265223972" style="display:none">I read this because several of my preteens/teens were reading it and I had not heard much about this title. <br />Dana is a quiet girl who spends all of her time with her friend Kai, a boy her age who can't be seen by anyone but Dana. At a young age, Dana is taken away by a strange man (with the consent of her parents). The man promises to keep her safe and feed her, which is more than her parents are able to guarantee. They travel for several days to the man's residence -- a lonely tower -- where the only other souls around are a dwarf who does the cooking and an elf, who is the only other student. <br />Dana is able to bring Kai with her, thanks to the magician, but many questions remain. Who is Kai, and more importantly, what is he? Why is Dana the only one who is able to see or hear him? Who is the magician and why are there so few students at the school? These unanswered questions keep the reader interested throughout the story, but I was disappointed by the lack of detail. Some might argue that most fantasy tales are too detail oriented, describing every mythological creature and magical item with thousands of words. That was not the case in The Valley of the Wolves. There is just enough detail to move the story along, but no more. There's very little description of the years of study between when Dana arrives as a little girl, and when most of the action takes place when she is 16. It's almost as if the first few chapters are simply a very long introduction, and the real story begins halfway through. <br />All in all, this was an interesting story that I would recommend to readers in grade 5 and up who just can't get enough fantasy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5093192282265223972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Eskana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4822415-eskana"><img alt="Eskana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339462379p2/4822415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977341668?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eskana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eskana" href="/user/show/4822415-eskana">Eskana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4822415-eskana?shelf=solid-fantasy">solid-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977341668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10855683030544434483">So, I originally read this book 8-9 nine years ago, and although I couldn't remember much about it, I remembered it being good and some of the characters. So, I thought, definitely something to re-read.<br/><br/>And I'm very glad I did! "The Valley of the Wolves" is a fantasy, but it is very unique. It centers on Dana, a young girl living on a grange who becomes the apprentice of a magus in the far-off Tower of the Valley of the Wolves. Dana is an alright character- quiet, independent, a little alone- but</span>
  <span id="freeText10855683030544434483" style="display:none">So, I originally read this book 8-9 nine years ago, and although I couldn't remember much about it, I remembered it being good and some of the characters. So, I thought, definitely something to re-read.<br /><br />And I'm very glad I did! "The Valley of the Wolves" is a fantasy, but it is very unique. It centers on Dana, a young girl living on a grange who becomes the apprentice of a magus in the far-off Tower of the Valley of the Wolves. Dana is an alright character- quiet, independent, a little alone- but I found her friend Kai to be one of the most memorable part of the book. This book has a lot of mystery in it, and Kai is one of them; he is Dana's best friend, who she's known almost her whole life, and yet, for some reason, no one else can see or hear him. Dana and Kai's relationship is easily one of the most fascinating parts of the book, and its growth throughout the story, along with Kai's mystery, is really cool to read.<br /><br />The mystery of the book, tangled as it is with magic, is very compelling, and told easily and quickly enough to keep a reader going (the author's writing style is easy to read, not high fantasy but well written.) The book starts with Dana's birth, but the author often jumps years between chapters, so that by the time the book is finished, she is sixteen. I think this helped skip the boring parts of learning spells and focus on the mystery, while also showing that neither magic nor mysteries are easy things to master.<br /><br />I can't say too much without giving away important plot points, but this book is definitely enjoyable, and definitely a recommended read. I was so excited to see that this is part of a series... can't wait to read the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10855683030544434483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

By the way, the world of the series is not enormous and doesnt have lots of lore and that stuff, but its quite good for young </span>
  <span id="freeText14945556924229875165" style="display:none">I started reading because of this book. Its the one that started me in the wonderful world of literature, so I love this book.<br />Its not one of the usual "starter books" as Harry Potter or so, although the story and the ingredients in the recipe are similar: a world full of magic, simple but different and charming characters, a bit of love, and a mistery or issue to unfold. By the way, the world of the series is not enormous and doesnt have lots of lore and that stuff, but its quite good for young readers: no too complex for them, but with cool details.<br />Its one of the first books the author Laura Gallego wrote, and you can notice that in the book, but even with that I enjoyed it really a lot.<br />If you have read other of Laura´s books (as Idhún for example), this will sound familiar to you, because other of her books have ideas, characters, or situations that are similar.<br />I would totally recommend it for young readers, even for kids that dont read. This might be the book to introduce your child to reading, as it was for me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16543814522468712567">I checked this book out of the library back when it first came out in English; it held me absolutely spellbound. So much so that three years later, I spent hours searching the library so I could read it again. Dana has a friend named Kai that no one else can see. Everyone assumes he isn't real, but one day, the Maestro offers her a school to attend; he can see Kai, too.<br/><br/>The farm scenes at the beginning, when it is just Dana and Kai, were the most beautiful for me; I loved envisioning her life. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText16543814522468712567" style="display:none">I checked this book out of the library back when it first came out in English; it held me absolutely spellbound. So much so that three years later, I spent hours searching the library so I could read it again. Dana has a friend named Kai that no one else can see. Everyone assumes he isn't real, but one day, the Maestro offers her a school to attend; he can see Kai, too.<br /><br />The farm scenes at the beginning, when it is just Dana and Kai, were the most beautiful for me; I loved envisioning her life. The ending both touched me and fascinated me. It's perfect for Harry Potter fans and fantasy lovers, though older readers may recognize the more stereotypical, trope-based parts that I missed as a younger, less experienced reader. A quick read, this book isn't challenging, but the prose is lovely and well-translated from the original Spanish. The poem in the beginning was a nice inclusion.</span>

<div id="review_2093321557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093321557" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7209591-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324262505p2/7209591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093321557?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/7209591-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093321557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2324568500449626644">This was another Women in Translation month read for me. This book reads like a fairy tale. There is a boy that only the girl can see. Is he real or not? <br/><br/>A magician comes and takes her away because he says that she will be a great magic user someday. He trains her in his castle that is surrounded by vicious wolves who come out at night. After years of training she realizes that she may not be able to leave if she doesn't figure out the secrets of the castle and the valley.<br/><br/>This book is all about </span>
  <span id="freeText2324568500449626644" style="display:none">This was another Women in Translation month read for me. This book reads like a fairy tale. There is a boy that only the girl can see. Is he real or not? <br /><br />A magician comes and takes her away because he says that she will be a great magic user someday. He trains her in his castle that is surrounded by vicious wolves who come out at night. After years of training she realizes that she may not be able to leave if she doesn't figure out the secrets of the castle and the valley.<br /><br />This book is all about growing up and seeing your life and the people in it for what they really are. It is a quick read with lots of fun fantasy and magical elements. <a href="http://www.spiritblog.net/some-of-the-things-i-havent-told-you/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on Based On A True Story</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer919827495" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13863755334479225712">The story starts with the main character, Dana as a small child whose friend, Kai, is someone only she can see. A circumstance that at first brings about fear and scorn from others, may be the reason why a magician has taken an interest in her, and offers to teacher her. Spanning the years from childhood to seeing Dana as a young woman, not everything is as it seems. Can she and Kai unravel the mystery of her new home? <br/><br/>Because of the shifts in time, some of Dana's changes in character can seem a</span>
  <span id="freeText13863755334479225712" style="display:none">The story starts with the main character, Dana as a small child whose friend, Kai, is someone only she can see. A circumstance that at first brings about fear and scorn from others, may be the reason why a magician has taken an interest in her, and offers to teacher her. Spanning the years from childhood to seeing Dana as a young woman, not everything is as it seems. Can she and Kai unravel the mystery of her new home? <br /><br />Because of the shifts in time, some of Dana's changes in character can seem abrupt, and we don't get to know any of the other characters as well. But the story still draws one in, and the characters make me anxious to find out if this book's two sequels have also been translated to English, as this book was. </span>

"The Valley of the Wolves" is a great fast-moving and compelling story filled with magic and mystery. <br/>For some reason I can't think of anything else to say... except to complain about Fenris, because that name is overused. And, if you know anything about Norse mythology, you might find this name to be at least a bit of a giveaway of what Fenris does later. Which is sad, because it kind of spoiled the surprise for</span>
  <span id="freeText7532796465607626226" style="display:none">Truly brilliant. The writing (well... the translator's writing, at least) is great. "The Valley of the Wolves" is a great fast-moving and compelling story filled with magic and mystery. <br />For some reason I can't think of anything else to say... except to complain about Fenris, because that name is overused. And, if you know anything about Norse mythology, you might find this name to be at least a bit of a giveaway of what Fenris does later. Which is sad, because it kind of spoiled the surprise for me, but it also left me with the satisfaction of knowing I was right. :P <br />I'll try to come up with more comments soon...</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28017475?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28017475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16450456855036209420">Since the age of 6, Dana has been able to see Kia - a boy that no one else can see or hear. A few years later, a sorcerer takes Dana as his apprentice. They travel to a tower in a valley filled with vicious wolves where for the next five years Dana learns magic. Before her final magic test, a golden lady appears and tells her to ‘find the unicorn.’ The mysteries of the golden lady, the valley, the sorcerer, a fellow apprentice and Kia’s true identity drive the plot to a startling conclusion. Dan</span>
  <span id="freeText16450456855036209420" style="display:none">Since the age of 6, Dana has been able to see Kia - a boy that no one else can see or hear. A few years later, a sorcerer takes Dana as his apprentice. They travel to a tower in a valley filled with vicious wolves where for the next five years Dana learns magic. Before her final magic test, a golden lady appears and tells her to ‘find the unicorn.’ The mysteries of the golden lady, the valley, the sorcerer, a fellow apprentice and Kia’s true identity drive the plot to a startling conclusion. Dana is an engaging character who tries to be a good person, but has faults such ignoring her feelings. There is a strong theme surrounding love and loyalty. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+XeHbrOcGS8jPbUyPSZhWKkO1cjvoefXsUI/QHn4NZ6OUvuEpp7RqSQkdahjVwMqDCpkTveHjG70Ah5MqxrX4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i0OL2LAATNpfplyy/Rg0YbbTYC9C1Jz9HaB4XSlueMX8ZvcypQKEXFi/nCijaVYTE/fRqVry90RY4FlR+4yaug==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a">About Laura Gallego García</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1398792330p3/228898.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/228898.Laura_Gallego_Garc_a">Laura Gallego García
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
4,645
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2888419226993344342">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br/><br/>Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began.</span>
  <span id="freeText2888419226993344342" style="display:none">Laura Gallego García is a Spanish author of fantasy and children's books. She studied Spanish Philology at the University of Valencia, and is currently working on her doctoral thesis. <br /><br />Her first novel, at the age of 21, was published because she won the Barco de Vapor literature prize and still is one of her most recognizable works: Finis Mundi. After that, her now stablished literary career began. <br /><br />Finis Mundi was followed, chronologically, by (only mentioning the ones that achieved notable popularity)the ''Crónicas de la Torre'' saga, ''The Legend of the Wandering King'', ''Memories of Idhún'' saga, ''La Emperatriz de los Etéreos'' and the ''Alas Negras'' saga. <br />From all of them, her most popular and internationally recognized work has been the Memorias de Idhún saga. Formed by three books, written between 2004 and 2006, the story (pure fantasy genre) centers in the three main characters: Victoria, Jack and Christian; and the world of Idhún. Dragons, unicorns, magic, prophecies and everything your imagination can lead you to. <br />The saga of Idhún and most of her works have been published to numerous languagues such as English, French, German, Italian, Hungarian, Greek, Portuguese, Corean, Polish, Swedish, Finish, Danish, Rumanian, Turkish...<br /><br />She loves manga comics. Her favourite book of all time is ''The Neverending Story'', though she enjoys reading as well authors such as Tolkien, Weis, Peter Beagle and Coehlo.<br /><br />Currently she combines being a mother and enjoying her family life with the realization of her thesis. She finished this year her last novel, ''Donde los árboles cantan'' (Where the trees sing), which will be published in October 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2888419226993344342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
